	<div class="content">
		<article class="article-container article--post ">
			<header class="article__header ">
	<div class="article__title-wrapper">
						<h1 class="article__title">3 views on the future of work, coffee shops and neighborhoods in a post-pandemic world</h1>
		</div>

			<div class="article__byline-wrapper">
			
<div class="article__byline">
						<a href="https://techcrunch.com/author/">
				Danny Crichton			</a>
					<a href="https://techcrunch.com/author/">
				Alex Wilhelm			</a>
					<a href="https://techcrunch.com/author/devin-coldewey/">
				Devin Coldewey			</a>
				<span class="article__byline__meta">
			2 days		</span>
	</div>
		</div>
	
			<div class="article__featured-image-wrapper breakout">
			<img src="https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/GettyImages-1154917433.jpg?w=533" class="article__featured-image" />
		</div>
	</header>

			<div class="article-content">
				<p id="speakable-summary"><span class="featured__span-first-words">The novel coronavirus</span> pandemic has disordered traditional notions of work, travel, socializing and the way we collaborate with colleagues.</p>
<p>It seems obvious that the future of work must evolve, given what we&#8217;re experiencing, but what will that future look like? Which changes are here to stay and which ones will revert the moment offices reopen?</p>
<p><a class="crunchbase-link" href="https://crunchbase.com/organization/techcrunch" target="_blank" data-type="organization" data-entity="techcrunch">TechCrunch <span class="crunchbase-tooltip-indicator"></span></a> has been a WFH employer for essentially its entire existence. Our staff is distributed across major startup hubs like SF and NYC, but we also have writers in smaller cities around the world, so we compiled reflections and thoughts from three of them about how remote work has changed our lifestyles and what we predict to see in the next few years, post-COVID 19.</p>
<p><a class="crunchbase-link" href="https://crunchbase.com/person/devin-coldewey" target="_blank" data-type="person" data-entity="devin-coldewey">Devin Coldewey <span class="crunchbase-tooltip-indicator"></span></a> talks about what’s going to change with coffee shops and co-working spaces, Alex Wilhelm discusses the future of the home office setup and Danny Crichton talks about the revitalization of urban and semi-urban neighborhoods.</p>
<h2>Devin Coldewey on coffee shops and more flexible work arrangements</h2>
<p>I&#8217;ve worked from home for over a decade and part of what makes it so lovely is the ability to do my work from a nearby cafe, or even a restaurant or bar. I&#8217;m lucky in that my part of the city is famously packed with excellent coffee shops, but in the time I&#8217;ve lived here I&#8217;ve seen them grow increasingly packed with — well, people like me. Some days they seem more like co-working spaces than cafes — and this is something business owners and neighborhoods are going to need to acknowledge one way or the other.</p>
<p>Most urban and suburban American communities were formed around the convention of commuting, which means fewer work-related resources where people live. Instead, we have all the restaurants, bodegas, thrift stores and all the other things that cater to people who aren&#8217;t working.<div class="extra-crunch-offer-container"></div>			</div>

							</footer>
		</article>
	</div>

ered":"Sorrento finds a coronavirus antibody that blocks viral infection 100% in preclinical lab experiments"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Therapeutics company Sorrento has made what it believes could be a breakthrough in potential treatment of SARS-CoV-2, the virus that leads to COVID-19. The company released details of its preclinical research on Friday, announcing that it has found an antibody that provides &#8220;100% inhibition of SARS-CoV-2 virus infection of healthy cells after four days incubation.&#8221; The results are from a preclinical study that still has to undergo peer review. It was an in vitro laboratory study (meaning not in an actual human being), but it&#8217;s still a promising development as the company continues to work on production of an antibody &#8220;cocktail&#8221; that could provide protection against SARS-CoV-2 even in case of mutations in the virus.<\/p>\n<p>Sorrento says it believes this antibody, which is labelled STI-1499, stood out among billions of candidates it has been screening from its extensive human antibody library for its ability to completely block the interaction of the SARS-CoV-2&#8217;s spike protein with a human cell target receptor. That means it prevents the virus from attaching to the host&#8217;s healthy cell, which is what leads to incubation and infection.<\/p>\n<p>The nature of the antibody&#8217;s efficacy means that Sorrento currently believes it will be the first antibody to be included in the cocktail it is developing, which will be made up of a large number of different antibodies that show efficacy in blocking the attachment of the spike protein, in order to provide multiple avenues of protection that are designed to remain effective even if the virus mutates in transmission from person to person, or within the same individual. One of the big outstanding questions that researchers are working on answering currently is just how mutagenic SARS-CoV-2 actually is, as many coronaviruses like the common cold show a tendency to mutate pretty quickly, rendering long-lasting cures and treatments difficult to develop.<\/p>\n<p>Sorrento&#8217;s COVID-SHIELD is meant to address this through a potent mix of different antibodies that provide protection against different strains of the virus, but the company says it also will be pursuing development of the STI-1499 antibody on its own as a dedicated, standalone therapy. The company is already in discussion with regulators about how to expedite development of that potential treatment, and is ramping its production capacity as well with the goal of producing as many as one million doses at the same time it pursues FDA approval for its use.<\/p>\n<p>It&#8217;s definitely worth cautioning that no treatment or vaccine is likely to be a &#8220;magic bullet&#8221; in treating SARS-CoV-2 or COVID-19, but this is still a promising development, and one to watch as it undergoes clinical trials and the therapeutic development and regulatory process.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/pages\/covid-19-updates\/\"><img src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/03\/covid-19-footer.png\" \/><\/a><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Therapeutics company Sorrento has made what it believes could be a breakthrough in potential treatment of SARS-CoV-2, the virus that leads to COVID-19. The company released details of its preclinical research on Friday, announcing that it has found an antibody that provides &#8220;100% inhibition of SARS-CoV-2 virus infection of healthy cells after four days incubation.&#8221; trade enters new era after overnight Huawei, Foxconn and TSMC announcements"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">There has been a steady drumbeat of news on the U.S.-China trade front since the start of the Trump administration. President Trump has made decoupling from China\u2019s economy on on-again, off-again proposition. There was the trade conflict with weekly changes in American tariff policy, the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/08\/07\/trump-huawei-zte-ban-tech\/\">threats against ZTE and Huawei<\/a>, the responses from China <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/07\/25\/qualcomm-says-it-will-terminate-its-massive-44b-offer-to-acquire-nxp\/\">against Qualcomm and NXP<\/a> and the launch of new restrictions on China investment in U.S. startups and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/06\/the-u-s-is-formalizing-team-telecom-rules-to-restrict-foreign-ownership-of-internet-and-telecom-assets\/\">telecom infrastructure<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>With COVID-19 and the ensuing global economic collapse, much of that conflict was put on the back burner. A tentative agreement between the U.S. and China \u2014 <a href=\"https:\/\/www.politico.com\/news\/2020\/01\/15\/what-is-in-us-china-trade-deal-099399\">agreed to before the worst of the pandemic<\/a> \u2014 seemed to get even broader support as the economic indicators from the globe\u2019s two superpowers started to trickle out.<\/p>\n<p>Then this week happened, and in almost no time at all, the U.S.-China trade detente has been torn apart.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Overnight, there were three critical stories that are going to reshape U.S.-China trade for the foreseeable future, with plenty more stories lurking beneath the surface.<\/p>\n<p>First, you have <a href=\"https:\/\/www.commerce.gov\/news\/press-releases\/2020\/05\/commerce-addresses-huaweis-efforts-undermine-entity-list-restricts\">the announcement this morning from the Department of Commerce<\/a> that the Trump administration is <a href=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/article\/us-usa-huawei-tech-exclusive\/u-s-moves-to-cut-huawei-off-from-global-chip-suppliers-idUSKBN22R1KC\">going to ban Huawei<\/a> from using U.S. software and hardware in certain strategic semiconductor processes, a move designed to limit the leading Chinese chip manufacturer from growing its market power and technological capabilities. Earlier yesterday, the administration also announced an <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/14\/trump-adds-another-year-to-huawei-zte-ban\/\">extension to the government\u2019s export ban on Huawei and ZTE<\/a>.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"kKUlXzZRqd\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/14\/trump-adds-another-year-to-huawei-zte-ban\/\">Trump adds another year to Huawei\/ZTE ban<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe title=\"&#8220;Trump adds another year to Huawei\/ZTE ban&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/14\/trump-adds-another-year-to-huawei-zte-ban\/embed\/#?secret=kKUlXzZRqd\" data-secret=\"kKUlXzZRqd\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>The Trump administration has threatened moves like this since almost the president\u2019s first day in office, and Commerce even couched the language, saying that it is \u201cnarrowly and strategically\u201d targeting the Chinese company. Nonetheless, Huawei\u2019s importance as one of China\u2019s leading technology companies can\u2019t be overstated, and the two moves combined is already being perceived as a direct assault on China\u2019s recovering economy.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Ta4ZCQdbtD\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/03\/28\/how-huawei-is-dividing-western-nations\/\">How Huawei is dividing Western nations<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe title=\"&#8220;How Huawei is dividing Western nations&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/03\/28\/how-huawei-is-dividing-western-nations\/embed\/#?secret=Ta4ZCQdbtD\" data-secret=\"Ta4ZCQdbtD\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Second, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/14\/tsmc-to-build-a-12-billion-advanced-semiconductor-plant-in-arizona-with-u-s-government-support\/\">you have a major announcement overnight from TSMC<\/a> \u2014 the world\u2019s largest chip foundry and one of the only foundries that can handle the manufacturing of the most advanced chips \u2014 that the Taiwanese company will <a href=\"https:\/\/www.tsmc.com\/tsmcdotcom\/PRListingNewsAction.do?action=detail&amp;language=E&amp;newsid=THGOANPGTH\">invest and launch a major, $12 billion factory in Arizona<\/a>. The release says that the factory will be capable of producing the world\u2019s most advanced 5-nanometer chips when it launches in a couple of years. The announcement came after weeks of debate in Washington aimed at cutting off TSMC\u2019s ability to build chips for mainland Chinese companies like Huawei \u2014 a move that TSMC argued would dramatically hurt its profitability and ability to invest in further R&amp;D.<\/p>\n<p>Third, you had the announcement this morning that <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/15\/foxconns-profits-plunged-nearly-90-due-to-covid-19-shutdown\/\">Foxconn\u2019s profits dived 90% due to COVID-19<\/a> and declining smartphone shipments. Foxconn, a Taiwanese hardware assembly company (among many other things), has been caught in the smoldering U.S.-China trade conflict, and even <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/02\/01\/foxconn-says-wisconsin-factory-plans-are-back-on-after-talk-with-trump\/\">attempted at one point to build its own $10 billion manufacturing facility in Wisconsin<\/a> with Trump\u2019s felicity <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/01\/30\/foxconn-pulls-back-on-its-10-billion-dollar-factory-commitment\/\">only to scuttle that plan entirely in an embarrassing setback<\/a>.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"TXxXGhJLeT\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/15\/foxconns-profits-plunged-nearly-90-due-to-covid-19-shutdown\/\">Foxconn\u2019s profits plunged nearly 90%, due to COVID-19 shutdown<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe title=\"&#8220;Foxconn\u2019s profits plunged nearly 90%, due to COVID-19 shutdown&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/15\/foxconns-profits-plunged-nearly-90-due-to-covid-19-shutdown\/embed\/#?secret=TXxXGhJLeT\" data-secret=\"TXxXGhJLeT\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Meanwhile, the trade deal that had calmed tensions between DC and Beijing <a href=\"https:\/\/www.cnbc.com\/2020\/05\/13\/trump-on-china-100-trade-deals-wouldnt-make-up-for-coronavirus.html\">appears increasingly in doubt<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>And that\u2019s just what happened <i>overnight<\/i>.<\/p>\n<p>There are so many individual data points on U.S.-China trade that it can be hard to see the patterns. Policies have hardened, policies have softened, but at its core the U.S. and China have attempted to keep the trade flowing, if only to maintain growth in their economies. That\u2019s what coupling has been all about: while there can be massive disagreements between the two sides, each has something the other wants. China wants to build and grow, while America wants to design and buy.<\/p>\n<p>The past few months of COVID-19 have changed that calculus, as has an election year in the United States, where <a href=\"https:\/\/www.pewresearch.org\/global\/2020\/04\/21\/u-s-views-of-china-increasingly-negative-amid-coronavirus-outbreak\/\">wariness of China has hit record, bipartisan highs, according to polls<\/a>. The intense conflagration of the American economy, with tens of millions jobless and growth stalled for the time being, means that even more intense scrutiny is being placed on anything that might be harming the country\u2019s financial math. We are now seeing the fruits of that new normal.<\/p>\n<p>There will be more decoupling maneuvers in the coming weeks. There will also almost certainly be a renegotiation of the U.S.-China trade deal, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.scmp.com\/news\/world\/united-states-canada\/article\/3084469\/coronavirus-donald-trump-threatens-cut-china-ties\">despite comments that neither side is interested in reopening those discussions<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Yet, the real interesting dynamic to watch is going to be Taiwan, which is home to strategically critical sectors of the chip industry. TSMC\u2019s announcement accepts the reality of decoupling, but attempts to work around it by <i>recoupling<\/i> the United States to the safety of Taiwan. Taiwanese companies and the island\u2019s politicians have avoided ceding its technology to other countries, creating a dependence that they have hoped would protect the island in the event of a mainland Chinese invasion. After all, if the Pentagon can\u2019t get its chips, it\u2019s going to have to intervene, or so the thinking holds.<\/p>\n<p>In this new world though, TSMC building an American factory doesn\u2019t undermine that narrative, it actually strengthens the bonds between the U.S. and Taiwan. More jobs, more trade, more travel and, ultimately, a deeper appreciation of the importance of each other. The question is how far the Trump administration is willing to go here. Taiwan is <a href=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/article\/us-health-coronavirus-taiwan\/taiwan-rejects-chinas-main-condition-for-who-participation-idUSKBN22R0HM\">bidding to rejoin the World Health Organization<\/a>, where it was an observer up to 2016. How deep are those ties? Will the U.S. go beyond its own diplomatic framework to intensely push for Taiwan\u2019s reentry in spite of Chinese opposition?<\/p>\n<p>That\u2019s what is next, but what is clear today is that the world of semiconductors, of internet infrastructure, of the tech ties that have bound the U.S. and China together for decades \u2014 they are frayed and are almost gone. It\u2019s a new era in supply chains and trade, and an open world for new approaches to these huge existing industries.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"eabHkB4dDX\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/13\/startups-are-transforming-global-trade-in-the-covid-19-era\/\">Startups are transforming global trade in the COVID-19 era<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe title=\"&#8220;Startups are transforming global trade in the COVID-19 era&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/13\/startups-are-transforming-global-trade-in-the-covid-19-era\/embed\/#?secret=eabHkB4dDX\" data-secret=\"eabHkB4dDX\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>There has been a steady drumbeat of news on the U.S.-China trade front since the start of the Trump administration. President Trump has made decoupling from China\u2019s economy on on-again, off-again proposition. to shop online that isn&#8217;t Amazon, Target or Walmart"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">As shutdown orders extend indefinitely, online shopping has become a lifeline for people forced to avoid the outside world. Often times opting to shop with a mega corporation like <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/organization\/amazon\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"amazon\">Amazon, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> Walmart or Target is the path of least resistance, but there are plenty of reasons to patronize an alternative.<\/p>\n<p>There are the ethical questions currently swirling around things like worker safety, as COVID-19 takes a toll on the often low-paid essential workers who keep these businesses running. It&#8217;s also arguably now more important than ever to support small and local businesses, and more and more brick and mortars announce that they simply won&#8217;t be able to rebound after the disastrous economic effects of the shutdown.<\/p>\n<p>Not every company listed below is a small business (Chewy, for example, is owned by pet supply giant PetSmart), but the below list compiled by our editorial team should offer a good variety to help you mix up your online shopping.<\/p>\n<h2>Groceries\/Household<\/h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1852652\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1852652\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-1852652\" https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/07\/GettyImages-1041147560-1.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/07\/GettyImages-1041147560-1.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-1852652\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">In this rear view, an unrecognizable woman stands with a shopping cart in front of a shelf full of food in the bread aisle of a grocery store.<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/thrivemarket.com\/\">Thrive Market:<\/a> Organic and non-GMO brands of food, home and beauty products, including healthy food, clean beauty and bath products, safe supplements and non-toxic home cleaner.<\/p>\n<p><em>Great for: Stocking up on healthier grocery items for the pantry and other household needs.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.grove.co\/\">Grove Collaborative:\u00a0<\/a>Eco-friendly home essentials, including cleaners, personal care, bath, baby\/kid and pet products.<\/p>\n<p><em>Great for: Stocking up on concentrated cleaners that reduce plastic waste and save trips to the store.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.boxed.com\/\">Boxed<\/a>: Online wholesale shopping on groceries, household products and health supplies.<\/p>\n<p><em>Great for: An online alternative to Costco and Sam&#8217;s Club for items you like to buy in bulk. (T.P. is often out-of-stock though!)\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"http:\/\/nuts.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https:\/\/www.google.com\/url?q=http:\/\/nuts.com\/&amp;source=gmail&amp;ust=1589742519422000&amp;usg=AFQjCNEeOZmj8UPcmiOd4_2njFGBzw8RDQ\">Nuts.com<\/a>: Grocery and dry goods items, focused on nuts and snacks<\/p>\n<p><em>Great for: Nuts, seeds, snacks, gluten-free flours, yeast, ceremonial-grade matcha powder, and hard-to-find spices.<\/em><\/p>\n<div><\/div>\n<h2>Pet Supplies<\/h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1575510\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1575510\" class=\"breakout size-full srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/12\/gettyimages-553927883-1.jpg 5228w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/12\/gettyimages-553927883-1.jpg?resize=150,102 class=\"wp-caption-text\">A pet cat asleep on the doormat in a conservatory.<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.chewy.com\/\">Chewy<\/a>: Online pet store offering food, toys, litter and other pet needs, including both over-the-counter medicine and prescriptions.<\/p>\n<p><em>Great for: High-quality foods and treats and skipping the vet for prescription refills.<\/em><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.thefarmersdog.com\/\">The Farmer&#8217;s Dog<\/a>: All-natural dog food delivery subscription service. Food is proportioned for your dog and delivered to your door.<\/p>\n<p><em>Great for: Fresh food delivery and those who want a &#8220;set it and forget it&#8221; option for buying dog food.<\/em><\/p>\n<h2>Beauty\/Baby Supplies<\/h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1825438\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1825438\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-1825438\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/GettyImages-78766213.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"685\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/GettyImages-78766213.jpg 5008w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/GettyImages-78766213.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/GettyImages-78766213.jpg?resize=300,201 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/GettyImages-78766213.jpg?resize=768,514 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/GettyImages-78766213.jpg?resize=680,455 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/GettyImages-78766213.jpg?resize=1536,1028 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/GettyImages-78766213.jpg?resize=2048,1371 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/GettyImages-78766213.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-1825438\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Vladmir Godnik \/ Getty Images<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.honest.com\/\">The Honest Company<\/a>: Ethical baby and beauty supply company.<\/p>\n<p><em>Great for: Diapers, baby needs and cruelty-free beauty, bath and body products.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.ulta.com\/\">Ulta<\/a>: Beauty supply superstore offering ship-to-home and curbside pickup.<\/p>\n<p><em>Great for: Makeup for your Zoom meetings; skincare products for all that indoor air you&#8217;re now living in.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.sephora.com\/\">Sephora<\/a>: Online beauty store offering direct shipping.<\/p>\n<p><em>Great for: Makeup, skincare and self-care items, as well as gift sets for someone who needs a boost.<\/em><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.glossier.com\/\">Glossier<\/a>: Online beauty brand that&#8217;s skin-first, makeup second.<\/p>\n<p><em>Great for: Skincare, body and makeup.<\/em><\/p>\n<h2>Books &amp; Entertainment<\/h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1453305\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1453305\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-1453305\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/02\/gettyimages-71553638.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"722\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/02\/gettyimages-71553638.jpg 2062w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/02\/gettyimages-71553638.jpg?resize=150,106 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/02\/gettyimages-71553638.jpg?resize=300,212 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/02\/gettyimages-71553638.jpg?resize=768,542 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/02\/gettyimages-71553638.jpg?resize=680,479 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/02\/gettyimages-71553638.jpg?resize=1536,1083 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/02\/gettyimages-71553638.jpg?resize=2048,1444 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/02\/gettyimages-71553638.jpg?resize=50,35 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-1453305\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Andersen Ross\/Blend Images<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/bookshop.org\/\">Bookshop.org: <\/a>This newly launched offering is designed specifically to support independent bookstores in a post-Amazon age. You can browse a wealth of titles and designate the specific store you want to support and they&#8217;ll get all the profits. With so many bookstores struggling to stay afloat well before the COVID pandemic, this could be Bookshop&#8217;s moment.<\/p>\n<p><em>Great for: Supporting independent bookstores while shopping online.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.powells.com\/\">Powell&#8217;s<\/a>: For book lovers, few things beat stepping foot inside this Portland mecca. Until things open back up, online shopping is the next best thing.<\/p>\n<p><em>Great for: Used books galore.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.amoeba.com\/\">Amoeba Records<\/a>: For psychical music releases, going straight to the label is often your best bet. Record stores are a great option, too. California&#8217;s Amoeba is one of the greatest small music chains in the world, but it&#8217;s among those with an uncertain post-COVID future, having recently announced the expected closure of its Hollywood location.<\/p>\n<p><em>Great for: New and used vinyl, CDs and books.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.fpnyc.com\/\">Forbidden Planet<\/a>: This Manhattan mainstay has become a go-to for mainstream and indie comics lovers alike. The store is one of countless currently struggling to stay afloat during the COVID crisis. They&#8217;ve started <a href=\"https:\/\/www.gofundme.com\/f\/help-forbidden-planet-nyc-survive\">a GoFundMe<\/a>, but better yet, go order some comics.<\/p>\n<p><em>Great for: Comics, from superhero to super indie.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.tridentbookscafe.com\/\">Trident Bookstore<\/a>: This gem of a Boston bookstore survived a fire and finals season, so you know it&#8217;s a special one. Its selling books all over the United States right now (and if you&#8217;re in Boston, it&#8217;ll add in brunch too).<\/p>\n<p><em>Great for: Well-known titles as well as undercover ones. Also, pro tip: You can purchase a &#8220;creative add-on&#8221; in your package like a surprise puzzle or a bundle of greeting cards, depending on availability.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n<h2>Athletic<\/h2>\n<p><img class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-1836934\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/06\/GettyImages-615919228.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/06\/GettyImages-615919228.jpg 5472w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/06\/GettyImages-615919228.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/06\/GettyImages-615919228.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"facebook\">Facebook <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> will acquire Giphy, the web-based animated gif search engine and platform provider, Facebook confirmed today, in a deal worth around $400 million, according to a report by\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/www.axios.com\/scoop-facebook-to-buy-giphy-for-400-million-4a75a359-833b-484d-b15b-87e94d3de017.html\">Axios<\/a>. Facebook said it isn&#8217;t disclosing terms of the deal. Giphy has grown to be a central source for shareable, high-engagement content, and its animated response gifs are available across Facebook&#8217;s platforms, as well as through other social apps and services on the web.<\/p>\n<p>Most notably, <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/organization\/giphy\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"giphy\">Giphy <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> provides built-in search and sticker functions for Facebook&#8217;s Instagram, and it will continue to operate in that capacity, becoming a part of the Instagram team. Giphy will also be available to Facebook&#8217;s other apps through existing and additional integrations. People will still be able to upload their own GIFs, and Facebook intends to continue to operate Giphy under its own branding and offer integration to outside developers.<\/p>\n<p>Facebook says it will invest in additional tech development for Giphy, as well as build out new relationships for it on both the content side and the endpoint developer side. The company says that fully 50% of traffic that Giphy receives already comes from Facebook&#8217;s apps, including Instagram, Messenger, the FB app itself and <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/organization\/whatsapp\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"whatsapp\">WhatsApp <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a>.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Giphy was founded in 2013, and was originally simply a search engine for gifs. The website&#8217;s first major product expansion was an extension that allowed sharing via Facebook, introduced later in its founding year, and it quickly added <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/organization\/twitter\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"twitter\">Twitter <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> as a second integration. According to the most recent data from <a href=\"https:\/\/www.crunchbase.com\/organization\/giphy\">Crunchbase<\/a>, Giphy had raised $150.9 million across five rounds, backed by funders including DFJ Growth, Lightspeed, Betaworks, GV, Lerer Hippeau and more.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Facebook will acquire Giphy, the web-based animated gif search engine and platform provider, Facebook confirmed today, in a deal worth around $400 million, according to a report by\u00a0Axios. Facebook said it isn&#8217;t disclosing terms of the deal. Giphy has grown to be a central source for shareable, high-engagement content, and its animated response gifs are class=\"contributor-byline__bio\">\n\t\tAnthony is co-founder and CEO of <a href=\"https:\/\/www.vinovest.co\/\">Vinovest<\/a>, a platform for investing in fine wine. He has previously founded and sold two companies (EnvoyNow &amp; Know Your VC), and is also a Thiel Fellow. \r\n\t<\/div>\n\t\n\t<\/div>\n<\/div><p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">The way we invest<\/span> is changing. Technology makes investing easy and more accessible than ever. Meanwhile, Millennials and Gen Z are <a href=\"https:\/\/www.cnbc.com\/2018\/08\/01\/why-millennials-are-scared-of-the-stock-market.html\">gravitating away from public equity investments<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>These changes have led to the rise of alternative assets. People are increasingly looking for new and innovative ways to approach investing. But are alternative assets truly the new frontier of modern investing?<\/p>\n<h2>What is an alternative asset?<\/h2>\n<p>As the name suggests, alternative assets are an alternative to traditional assets, like stock, bonds and cash. The term usually describes unconventional investments. That can include anything from a <a href=\"https:\/\/www.beckett.com\/news\/world-record-price-for-t206-honus-wagner-baseball-card-3-million-and-counting\/\">Honus Wagner baseball card<\/a> to <a href=\"https:\/\/www.winespectator.com\/articles\/harlan-estate-screaming-eagle-top-napa-valley-wine-auction-20673\">bottles of fine wine<\/a>. However, it can also apply to more familiar investments, like real estate and private mortgages.<\/p>\n<p>Simply put: alternative assets are the things that probably wouldn\u2019t come up when you meet with your financial advisor. They are not easily categorizable, which makes them more difficult to manage. Often, people invest in alternative assets because of a passion for the asset rather than the immediate ROI.<\/p>\n<h2>What makes alternative assets an attractive investment?<\/h2>\n<p>Investors will go wherever there is money to be made. That includes alternative assets. In addition to <a href=\"https:\/\/www.cfainstitute.org\/en\/membership\/professional-development\/refresher-readings\/2020\/introduction-alternative-investments\">higher potential returns<\/a>, alternative assets have distinct characteristics from traditional assets. Here are a couple of factors to consider when looking at alternative assets:<\/p>\n<h3>Portfolio Diversification<div After watching the stock market take yet another <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/03\/16\/stock-markets-halted-for-third-time-as-heavy-selling-trips-circuit-breakers-due-to-coronavirus-scare\/\">unprecedented nosedive<\/a> due to coronavirus, she called up a potential investor.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cIf this isn\u2019t going to happen, let\u2019s call it now,\u201d Yancey said, referring to the close of her Series A round, the first capital her culture tech company, <a href=\"https:\/\/emtrain.com\/\">Emtrain<\/a>, would have accepted in 14 years. \u201cAt that point, I put my nose to the grindstone; I didn\u2019t have a lot of bandwidth in engaging in conversation that wasn\u2019t going anywhere.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>She had the conversation on Monday, and the deal closed on Friday. \u201cI remember thinking, &#8216;this is the only deal that is happening this month,&#8217; \u201d she recalled.<\/p>\n<p>As lockdowns extend to prevent the spread of the coronavirus, investors and startups are searching for new ways to connect with each other. VCs stacked billions in Q1 while smaller firms saw their haul shrink"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">Hello and welcome<\/span> back to our regular morning look at private companies, public markets and the gray space in between.<\/p>\n<p>After spending perhaps more time than we should have recently <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/14\/are-stable-saas-valuations-driven-by-logic-or-hope\/\">trying to figure out what&#8217;s going on with the public markets<\/a>, let&#8217;s return to the private markets this morning, focusing in on venture capital itself. New data out today details how U.S.-based VCs fared in Q1 2020, giving us a window into how flush the financial class of startup land was heading into the COVID-19 era.<\/p>\n<p>The short answer is that big funds raised lots of cash, while smaller funds appear to have put in a somewhat lackluster quarter.<\/p>\n<p>That big funds performed well in Q1 shouldn&#8217;t surprise. We&#8217;ve seen <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/01\/17\/the-paradox-of-2020-vc-is-that-the-largest-funds-are-doing-the-smallest-rounds\/\">NEA stack $3.6 billion in March<\/a>\u00a0and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/02\/19\/founders-fund-confirms-3-billion-in-new-capital-across-two-funds\/\">Founders Fund raised $3 billion for its own investing work<\/a> earlier in the quarter, to pick two examples TechCrunch covered.<\/p>\n<p>The impact of these mega-raises, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.firstrepublic.com\/-\/media\/frb\/documents\/pdfs\/innovators\/preqin-and-first-republic-update-us-venture-capital-in-q1-2020_v2.pdf?cmpid=Email_VC%20Report%20Q1%20May%202020%20-%20Samir%20(1)_&amp;spMailingID=42493879&amp;spUserID=NzY0NDY3MjM5NjkS1&amp;spJobID=1761303926&amp;spReportId=MTc2MTMwMzkyNgS2\">according to a report from Prequin and First Republic Bank<\/a>, was to push up the total amount of capital raised by American venture capital firms in the quarter, while the decline in the number of funds that raised $50 million or less led to a slim number of total funds raised. It&#8217;s hard to call a surge in dry powder bearish, but the fall-off on smaller funds could limit seed capital in the future.<\/p>\n<p>Notably, there have been <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/09\/10\/where-have-all-the-seed-deals-gone\/\">warning signs since at least 2019<\/a> that seed volume was slowing; <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/14\/vc-activity-goes-upside-down-as-seed-deals-fall-and-mega-rounds-rise\/\">recent data from the U.S. underscores the trend<\/a>. So what we&#8217;re seeing this morning in data-form is a summation of what we&#8217;ve previously reported in a more piecemeal fashion.<\/p>\n<p>Let&#8217;s pick over the data to see what we can learn about how much spare capital the venture classes are sitting on today.<\/p>\n<h2>The rich get richer<\/h2>\n<p>The <a href=\"https:\/\/www.firstrepublic.com\/-\/media\/frb\/documents\/pdfs\/innovators\/preqin-and-first-republic-update-us-venture-capital-in-q1-2020_v2.pdf?cmpid=Email_VC%20Report%20Q1%20May%202020%20-%20Samir%20(1)_&amp;spMailingID=42493879&amp;spUserID=NzY0NDY3MjM5NjkS1&amp;spJobID=1761303926&amp;spReportId=MTc2MTMwMzkyNgS2\">whole report<\/a> is worth reading if you have time. Aside from the data concerning how much money VCs are raising themselves, it includes several interesting bits of information. For example, there were just 960 venture deals closed in the U.S. in Q1 &#8212; a pace that would make 2020 the slowest year since 2009 if it held steady.<\/p>\n<p>Per the listed data, 83 U.S.-based venture capitalists closed (&#8220;held a final close&#8221;) a fund in Q1 2020. This was off about 24% from the Q1 2019 result of 109. However, while the number of funds raised was lackluster, they made up for it in dollar-scale. According to <a href=\"https:\/\/www.preqin.com\/\">Preqin<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.firstrepublic.com\/\">First Republic Bank<\/a>, the &#8220;funds that closed raised $27 [billion], a substantial total representing over half of the capital raised in 2019 ($50 [billion]).&#8221;<div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"><\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Hello and welcome back to our regular morning look at private companies, public markets and the gray space in between. After spending perhaps more time than we should have recently trying to figure out what&#8217;s going on with the public markets, let&#8217;s return to the private markets this morning, focusing in on venture capital itself. top mobility VCs discuss COVID-19 strategies and trends"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">As COVID-19 swept<\/span> across the globe, no sector lay untouched, but perhaps no industry was more disrupted than transportation.<\/p>\n<p>Airlines slashed routes, public transit use plummeted, ridership on <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/organization\/uber\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"uber\">Uber, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> Lyft and other ride-hailing platforms dropped and shared scooter companies pulled products from city streets. Meanwhile, e-bike sales bloomed and on-demand delivery, including services using autonomous robots, exploded.<\/p>\n<p>Transportation companies have been forced to adapt \u2014 quickly \u2014 to this new reality. Uber, for example, found itself in a position where it felt both right to <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/06\/uber-is-laying-off-3700-as-rides-plummet-due-to-covid-19\/\">lay off thousands of employees <\/a>as it planned to <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/06\/uber-is-laying-off-3700-as-rides-plummet-due-to-covid-19\/\">inject $170 million into micromobility startup Lime<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>The upshot: Along with the pain, crises can also be a catalyst for innovation. TechCrunch spoke to seven venture capitalists about how COVID-19 affected their portfolio and investment strategy, and asked their advice for startup founders as well as where they think the next and overlooked hot opportunity will be:<\/p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/www.alsop-louie.com\/team\/ernestine-fu\/\">Ernestine Fu<\/a>, Alsop Louie Partners<\/li>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/urban.us\/about-us\/stonly-baptiste\/\">Stonly Baptiste<\/a> &amp; <a href=\"https:\/\/urban.us\/about-us\/shaun-abrahamson\/\">Shaun Abrahamson<\/a>, Urban.us<\/li>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/shastaventures.com\/team\/rob-coneybeer\/\">Rob Coneybeer<\/a>, Shasta Ventures<\/li>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/luxcapital.com\/team\/shahin-farshchi\/\">Shahin Farshchi<\/a>, Lux Capital<\/li>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/in\/k8schox\">Kate Schox<\/a>, Trucks VC<\/li>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/www.autotechvc.com\/team\">Jeff Peters<\/a>, Autotech Ventures<\/li>\n<\/ul>\n<h2>Ernestine Fu, Alsop Louie Partners<\/h2>\n<p><strong>How has COVID-19 impacted your investment strategy?\u00a0<\/strong><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Early-stage venture capital is about investing in the steady growth and potential of a business over time. We\u2019re in it for the long term, and the economy will eventually rebound. We\u2019re preserving dry powder for existing investments, but at the same time, I\u2019m reminded that some of the best venture-backed businesses were founded and funded during recessionary times (e.g. Google, Salesforce, Instagram). So we\u2019re keeping our eyes open for promising young startups too.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><b>What is your advice to startups in your portfolio right now?<\/b><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">COVID-19 is an existential event in all of our lives and businesses. Stay positive and be empathetic \u2014 protect your employees and communicate often, maintain the financial health of your business and know you need to adapt to the change that will continue to happen. <div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"><\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>As COVID-19 swept across the globe, no sector lay untouched, but perhaps no industry was more disrupted than transportation. views on the future of work, coffee shops and neighborhoods in a post-pandemic world"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">The novel coronavirus<\/span> pandemic has disordered traditional notions of work, travel, socializing and the way we collaborate with colleagues.<\/p>\n<p>It seems obvious that the future of work must evolve, given what we&#8217;re experiencing, but what will that future look like? Which changes are here to stay and which ones will revert the moment offices reopen?<\/p>\n<p><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/organization\/techcrunch\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"techcrunch\">TechCrunch <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> has been a WFH employer for essentially its entire existence. Our staff is distributed across major startup hubs like SF and NYC, but we also have writers in smaller cities around the world, so we compiled reflections and thoughts from three of them about how remote work has changed our lifestyles and what we predict to see in the next few years, post-COVID 19.<\/p>\n<p><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/person\/devin-coldewey\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"devin-coldewey\">Devin Coldewey <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> talks about what\u2019s going to change with coffee shops and co-working spaces, Alex Wilhelm discusses the future of the home office setup and Danny Crichton talks about the revitalization of urban and semi-urban neighborhoods.<\/p>\n<h2>Devin Coldewey on coffee shops and more flexible work arrangements<\/h2>\n<p>I&#8217;ve worked from home for over a decade and part of what makes it so lovely is the ability to do my work from a nearby cafe, or even a restaurant or bar. I&#8217;m lucky in that my part of the city is famously packed with excellent coffee shops, but in the time I&#8217;ve lived here I&#8217;ve seen them grow increasingly packed with \u2014 well, people like me. Some days they seem more like co-working spaces than cafes \u2014 and this is something business owners and neighborhoods are going to need to acknowledge one way or the other.<\/p>\n<p>Most urban and suburban American communities were formed around the convention of commuting, which means fewer work-related resources where people live. Instead, we have all the restaurants, bodegas, thrift stores and all the other things that cater to people who aren&#8217;t working.<div views on the future of work, coffee shops and neighborhoods in a post-pandemic world"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">The novel coronavirus<\/span> pandemic has disordered traditional notions of work, travel, socializing and the way we collaborate with colleagues.<\/p>\n<p>It seems obvious that the future of work must evolve, given what we&#8217;re experiencing, but what will that future look like? Which changes are here to stay and which ones will revert the moment offices reopen?<\/p>\n<p><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/organization\/techcrunch\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"techcrunch\">TechCrunch <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> has been a WFH employer for essentially its entire existence. Our staff is distributed across major startup hubs like SF and NYC, but we also have writers in smaller cities around the world, so we compiled reflections and thoughts from three of them about how remote work has changed our lifestyles and what we predict to see in the next few years, post-COVID 19.<\/p>\n<p><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https:\/\/crunchbase.com\/person\/devin-coldewey\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"devin-coldewey\">Devin Coldewey <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"><\/span><\/a> talks about what\u2019s going to change with coffee shops and co-working spaces, Alex Wilhelm discusses the future of the home office setup and Danny Crichton talks about the revitalization of urban and semi-urban neighborhoods.<\/p>\n<h2>Devin Coldewey on coffee shops and more flexible work arrangements<\/h2>\n<p>I&#8217;ve worked from home for over a decade and part of what makes it so lovely is the ability to do my work from a nearby cafe, or even a restaurant or bar. I&#8217;m lucky in that my part of the city is famously packed with excellent coffee shops, but in the time I&#8217;ve lived here I&#8217;ve seen them grow increasingly packed with \u2014 well, people like me. Some days they seem more like co-working spaces than cafes \u2014 and this is something business owners and neighborhoods are going to need to acknowledge one way or the other.<\/p>\n<p>Most urban and suburban American communities were formed around the convention of commuting, which means fewer work-related resources where people live. Instead, we have all the restaurants, bodegas, thrift stores and all the other things that cater to people who aren&#8217;t working.<div
